<!-- ═══════════════════════════════════════════ -->

<div class="ta-screen" id="s-learn">
  <div class="learn-intro">
    Welcome to <strong style="color:var(--green)">TA School</strong> — everything you need to read charts like a professional. Each lesson teaches you exactly what traders look for and how to act on it.
  </div>

  <!-- 01 Candlesticks -->

  <div class="learn-card">
    <div class="learn-hdr" onclick="toggleLearn(this)">
      <div class="learn-icon">🕯️</div>
      <div class="learn-title">HOW TO READ CANDLESTICKS</div>
      <div class="learn-tag">FOUNDATION</div>
      <div class="learn-arrow">›</div>
    </div>
    <div class="learn-body">
      <h3>THE CANDLESTICK</h3>
      <p>Every candle represents one time period (1 day in our charts). The <strong style="color:var(--tx)">body</strong> shows where price opened and closed. The <strong style="color:var(--tx)">wicks</strong> show the extreme high and low reached during that period.</p>
      <div class="candle-legend">
        <div class="candle-item">
          <div class="candle-visual">
            <div class="candle-wick" style="background:var(--green);top:0;height:5px"></div>
            <div class="candle-body" style="background:var(--green);top:5px;height:14px"></div>
            <div class="candle-wick" style="background:var(--green);top:19px;height:5px"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="candle-label">BULLISH<br/>(Close > Open)</div>
        </div>
        <div class="candle-item">
          <div class="candle-visual">
            <div class="candle-wick" style="background:var(--red);top:0;height:5px"></div>
            <div class="candle-body" style="background:var(--red);top:5px;height:14px"></div>
            <div class="candle-wick" style="background:var(--red);top:19px;height:5px"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="candle-label">BEARISH<br/>(Close < Open)</div>
        </div>
      </div>
      <h3>KEY PATTERNS TO RECOGNIZE</h3>
      <div class="learn-rule">
        <div class="rule-title">🔨 HAMMER — Reversal Signal</div>
        <div class="rule-body">Long lower wick, small body at top. Means sellers pushed price down hard, but buyers stepped in and pushed it back up. Bullish reversal signal especially after a downtrend.</div>
      </div>
      <div class="learn-rule" style="border-color:var(--red)">
        <div class="rule-title" style="color:var(--red)">⭐ DOJI — Indecision</div>
        <div class="rule-body">Open and close nearly equal. Neither bulls nor bears in control. Often appears before a reversal. Context matters — a doji after an uptrend can signal a top.</div>
      </div>
      <div class="learn-rule">
        <div class="rule-title">🌅 BULLISH ENGULFING — Strong Reversal</div>
        <div class="rule-body">A large green candle completely engulfs the previous red candle. One of the most reliable reversal signals. Strong buying pressure overwhelming selling.</div>
      </div>
      <div class="learn-rule" style="border-color:var(--amber)">
        <div class="rule-title" style="color:var(--amber)">⭐ SPINNING TOP — Indecision</div>
        <div class="rule-body">Small body with wicks on both sides. Means the market is undecided. Not actionable alone — wait for the next candle to confirm direction.</div>
      </div>
      <p><strong style="color:var(--tx)">Rule:</strong> Never trade a single candle in isolation. Always look at the last 5–10 candles together to understand the story.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <!-- 02 RSI -->

  <div class="learn-card">
    <div class="learn-hdr" onclick="toggleLearn(this)">
      <div class="learn-icon">📊</div>
      <div class="learn-title">RSI — RELATIVE STRENGTH INDEX</div>
      <div class="learn-tag">MOMENTUM</div>
      <div class="learn-arrow">›</div>
    </div>
    <div class="learn-body">
      <h3>WHAT IS RSI?</h3>
      <p>RSI measures <strong style="color:var(--tx)">momentum</strong> — how fast and how strongly a stock is moving. It oscillates between 0 and 100. Created by J. Welles Wilder. Uses 14 periods by default.</p>
      <div class="zone-row">
        <div class="zone-box zone-oversold"><div class="zb-label">OVERSOLD</div><div class="zb-range">0–30</div><div class="zb-action">Potential buy zone</div></div>
        <div class="zone-box zone-neutral"><div class="zb-label">NEUTRAL</div><div class="zb-range">30–70</div><div class="zb-action">No signal</div></div>
        <div class="zone-box zone-overbought"><div class="zb-label">OVERBOUGHT</div><div class="zb-range">70–100</div><div class="zb-action">Potential sell zone</div></div>
      </div>
      <div class="learn-rule">
        <div class="rule-title">🎯 HOW TO USE RSI — THE RIGHT WAY</div>
        <div class="rule-body">RSI below 30 = oversold. This means the asset has been sold heavily and may bounce. But oversold doesn't mean "buy immediately" — it means "pay attention." Wait for RSI to turn back UP from oversold before entering.</div>
      </div>
      <h3>RSI DIVERGENCE — THE HIDDEN SIGNAL</h3>
      <p><strong style="color:var(--green)">Bullish Divergence:</strong> Price makes a lower low, but RSI makes a higher low. This means selling momentum is weakening even as price falls. Strong buy signal.</p>
      <p><strong style="color:var(--red)">Bearish Divergence:</strong> Price makes a higher high, but RSI makes a lower high. Momentum is weakening. Strong sell/take profit signal.</p>
      <div class="learn-rule" style="border-color:var(--amber)">
        <div class="rule-title" style="color:var(--amber)">⚠️ RSI MISTAKE TO AVOID</div>
        <div class="rule-body">Don't buy just because RSI is at 30. In a strong downtrend, RSI can stay under 30 for weeks. Always combine RSI with trend (EMA) and volume confirmation.</div>
      </div>
    </div>
  </div>

  <!-- 03 MACD -->

  <div class="learn-card">
    <div class="learn-hdr" onclick="toggleLearn(this)">
      <div class="learn-icon">📉</div>
      <div class="learn-title">MACD — MOVING AVG CONVERGENCE/DIVERGENCE</div>
      <div class="learn-tag">MOMENTUM</div>
      <div class="learn-arrow">›</div>
    </div>
    <div class="learn-body">
      <h3>WHAT IS MACD?</h3>
      <p>MACD shows the relationship between two moving averages. It has three components:</p>
      <ul>
        <li><strong style="color:var(--blue)">MACD Line</strong> = EMA(12) minus EMA(26). The fast line.</li>
        <li><strong style="color:var(--amber)">Signal Line</strong> = EMA(9) of the MACD line. The slow line.</li>
        <li><strong style="color:var(--green)">Histogram</strong> = MACD minus Signal. Shows momentum strength.</li>
      </ul>
      <div class="learn-rule">
        <div class="rule-title">🟢 BULLISH CROSSOVER — Buy Signal</div>
        <div class="rule-body">MACD line crosses ABOVE the signal line. This is one of the most commonly watched buy signals. The histogram turns positive. Strongest when it happens below the zero line (in negative territory).</div>
      </div>
      <div class="learn-rule" style="border-color:var(--red)">
        <div class="rule-title" style="color:var(--red)">🔴 BEARISH CROSSOVER — Sell Signal</div>
        <div class="rule-body">MACD line crosses BELOW the signal line. Strongest when it happens above the zero line. Combined with RSI overbought = high-conviction exit signal.</div>
      </div>
      <div class="learn-rule" style="border-color:var(--amber)">
        <div class="rule-title" style="color:var(--amber)">📊 HISTOGRAM READING</div>
        <div class="rule-body">Green bars growing = bullish momentum building. Green bars shrinking = momentum fading (potential sell). Red bars growing = bearish momentum. Red bars shrinking = selling pressure easing (potential buy).</div>
      </div>
      <p><strong style="color:var(--tx)">MACD is a lagging indicator.</strong> It confirms trends rather than predicting them. Best used alongside RSI and volume for entry timing.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <!-- 04 Bollinger Bands -->

  <div class="learn-card">
    <div class="learn-hdr" onclick="toggleLearn(this)">
      <div class="learn-icon">🎯</div>
      <div class="learn-title">BOLLINGER BANDS — VOLATILITY SIGNALS</div>
      <div class="learn-tag">VOLATILITY</div>
      <div class="learn-arrow">›</div>
    </div>
    <div class="learn-body">
      <h3>WHAT ARE BOLLINGER BANDS?</h3>
      <p>Three lines: a 20-day moving average in the middle, with upper and lower bands at ±2 standard deviations. They expand when volatility is high and contract when it's low.</p>
      <div class="learn-rule">
        <div class="rule-title">🔥 THE BOLLINGER SQUEEZE</div>
        <div class="rule-body">When bands get very narrow (squeeze), it signals low volatility — and low volatility is always followed by HIGH volatility. A squeeze is like a coiled spring. Watch for the breakout direction after a squeeze. Volume confirms which way it goes.</div>
      </div>
      <div class="learn-rule">
        <div class="rule-title">🎯 MEAN REVERSION</div>
        <div class="rule-body">Price touching the lower band doesn't mean buy. It means price is 2 standard deviations below average — statistically unusual. In ranging markets, price tends to revert to the middle band. In trending markets, price can "walk the band" for extended periods.</div>
      </div>
      <ul>
        <li>Price touching <strong style="color:var(--red)">lower band</strong> + RSI oversold = potential entry zone</li>
        <li>Price touching <strong style="color:var(--green)">upper band</strong> + RSI overbought = potential exit zone</li>
        <li>Price breaking outside the band on high volume = strong momentum move</li>
        <li>Bands squeezing = watch for breakout, size your position accordingly</li>
      </ul>
    </div>
  </div>

  <!-- 05 EMAs -->

  <div class="learn-card">
    <div class="learn-hdr" onclick="toggleLearn(this)">
      <div class="learn-icon">📈</div>
      <div class="learn-title">EMAs — THE TREND BACKBONE</div>
      <div class="learn-tag">TREND</div>
      <div class="learn-arrow">›</div>
    </div>
    <div class="learn-body">
      <h3>EMA vs SMA</h3>
      <p>EMA (Exponential Moving Average) weights recent prices more than older ones. It reacts faster than SMA (Simple Moving Average). We use EMA20, EMA50, and EMA200.</p>
      <div class="learn-rule">
        <div class="rule-title" style="color:#ffd700">📊 EMA 20 — Short-term trend</div>
        <div class="rule-body">Shows the trend of the last 4 weeks. Price above EMA20 = short-term bullish. Many traders use EMA20 as a trailing stop — if price closes below it, they exit a short-term position.</div>
      </div>
      <div class="learn-rule" style="border-color:#ff8c00">
        <div class="rule-title" style="color:#ff8c00">📊 EMA 50 — Medium-term trend</div>
        <div class="rule-body">The most-watched moving average by institutional traders. Price above EMA50 = medium-term bullish. A bounce off EMA50 after a pullback in an uptrend is a classic high-probability buy setup.</div>
      </div>
      <div class="learn-rule" style="border-color:#ff4444">
        <div class="rule-title" style="color:#ff4444">📊 EMA 200 — The Long Game</div>
        <div class="rule-body">The most important moving average for long-term investors. Price above EMA200 = bull market. Price below EMA200 = bear market. This one line separates risk-on from risk-off for major institutional allocations.</div>
      </div>
      <h3>GOLDEN CROSS &amp; DEATH CROSS</h3>
      <p><strong style="color:var(--green)">Golden Cross:</strong> EMA50 crosses above EMA200. Historically one of the most bullish signals in all of TA. Institutional buying often follows.</p>
      <p><strong style="color:var(--red)">Death Cross:</strong> EMA50 crosses below EMA200. Strong bear signal. Can precede significant declines.</p>
      <h3>EMA ALIGNMENT — THE BULL STACK</h3>
      <p>When price &gt; EMA20 &gt; EMA50 &gt; EMA200, all trend indicators are aligned bullish. This is called the "bull stack." The strongest, cleanest uptrends have this alignment throughout.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <!-- 06 Support & Resistance -->

  <div class="learn-card">
    <div class="learn-hdr" onclick="toggleLearn(this)">
      <div class="learn-icon">🧱</div>
      <div class="learn-title">SUPPORT &amp; RESISTANCE — THE MAP</div>
      <div class="learn-tag">STRUCTURE</div>
      <div class="learn-arrow">›</div>
    </div>
    <div class="learn-body">
      <h3>WHAT ARE THEY?</h3>
      <p><strong style="color:var(--green)">Support:</strong> A price level where buyers have historically stepped in, preventing further decline. Think of it as the floor.</p>
      <p><strong style="color:var(--red)">Resistance:</strong> A price level where sellers have historically stepped in, preventing further advance. Think of it as the ceiling.</p>
      <div class="learn-rule">
        <div class="rule-title">🔄 ROLE REVERSAL — The Most Powerful Concept</div>
        <div class="rule-body">When price breaks through resistance, that resistance level often becomes the new support. When support breaks, it becomes new resistance. This is called "role reversal" and is one of the most reliable setups in TA.</div>
      </div>
      <ul>
        <li>The more times a level is tested and holds, the stronger it is</li>
        <li>High-volume tests at a level = stronger support/resistance</li>
        <li>Round numbers ($100, $200, $50,000 BTC) act as psychological S/R</li>
        <li>52-week highs and lows are always strong S/R levels</li>
        <li>Previous ATH (all-time high) is always major resistance until broken</li>
      </ul>
      <h3>HOW TO USE IT FOR ENTRIES</h3>
      <p>Buy near confirmed support with a stop loss just below it. The best risk/reward entries are when price pulls back to a strong support level in an overall uptrend. Risk is defined and small, reward is potentially large.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <!-- 07 Fibonacci -->

  <div class="learn-card">
    <div class="learn-hdr" onclick="toggleLearn(this)">
      <div class="learn-icon">🌀</div>
      <div class="learn-title">FIBONACCI RETRACEMENTS</div>
      <div class="learn-tag">STRUCTURE</div>
      <div class="learn-arrow">›</div>
    </div>
    <div class="learn-body">
      <h3>THE GOLDEN RATIO IN MARKETS</h3>
      <p>After a strong move up, price rarely goes straight. It retraces (pulls back) a predictable percentage before continuing higher. Fibonacci levels identify where those pullbacks tend to stop.</p>
      <div class="learn-rule">
        <div class="rule-title">📐 KEY FIBONACCI LEVELS</div>
        <div class="rule-body">
          <strong style="color:var(--green)">23.6%</strong> — Shallow retracement. Strong uptrend. Weak hands shaken out.<br/>
          <strong style="color:var(--green)">38.2%</strong> — Most common retracement level. Good first entry zone.<br/>
          <strong style="color:var(--amber)">50.0%</strong> — Psychological level. Not Fibonacci but widely watched.<br/>
          <strong style="color:var(--amber)">61.8%</strong> — The "Golden Ratio." Deepest common retracement. Strong support.<br/>
          <strong style="color:var(--red)">78.6%</strong> — Deep retracement. Structure weakening. Last-chance support.
        </div>
      </div>
      <p>The 38.2% and 61.8% levels are where most professional traders place limit orders. If a stock is in a clear uptrend and pulls back to these levels, it's a high-probability entry zone.</p>
      <p><strong style="color:var(--tx)">How we draw it:</strong> Find the most recent significant swing low to swing high (for an uptrend). The Fibonacci tool draws percentage levels from that range.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <!-- 08 Volume -->

  <div class="learn-card">
    <div class="learn-hdr" onclick="toggleLearn(this)">
      <div class="learn-icon">📦</div>
      <div class="learn-title">VOLUME — THE TRUTH TELLER</div>
      <div class="learn-tag">CONFIRMATION</div>
      <div class="learn-arrow">›</div>
    </div>
    <div class="learn-body">
      <h3>WHY VOLUME MATTERS MORE THAN PRICE</h3>
      <p>Price tells you what happened. Volume tells you how much conviction was behind it. A price move on low volume may be fake. A price move on massive volume is real and significant.</p>
      <ul>
        <li><strong style="color:var(--green)">Price up + Volume up</strong> = Strong buying. Trend confirmed.</li>
        <li><strong style="color:var(--red)">Price up + Volume down</strong> = Weak rally. May not last.</li>
        <li><strong style="color:var(--green)">Price down + Volume down</strong> = Pullback on low conviction. Healthy in uptrend.</li>
        <li><strong style="color:var(--red)">Price down + Volume up</strong> = Heavy selling. Distribution. Bearish.</li>
      </ul>
      <div class="learn-rule">
        <div class="rule-title">💡 VOLUME SPIKE = ATTENTION SIGNAL</div>
        <div class="rule-body">When volume is 5x+ the 30-day average, something significant is happening — whether good or bad. This is the most reliable early-warning signal for major moves. For microcaps like CLOV, a volume spike is often the first sign institutions are accumulating.</div>
      </div>
      <h3>OBV — ON-BALANCE VOLUME</h3>
      <p>OBV adds volume on up days and subtracts on down days. A rising OBV while price is flat or slightly down = accumulation happening (smart money buying). This often precedes a price breakout.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <!-- 09 How to Build a Buy Plan -->

  <div class="learn-card">
    <div class="learn-hdr" onclick="toggleLearn(this)">
      <div class="learn-icon">🎯</div>
      <div class="learn-title">HOW TO BUILD A BUY PLAN</div>
      <div class="learn-tag">STRATEGY</div>
      <div class="learn-arrow">›</div>
    </div>
    <div class="learn-body">
      <h3>THE 3-LEVEL STAGED ENTRY</h3>
      <p>Never go all-in at one price. Professional investors split entries into 3 tranches. This ensures you get a cost average that works regardless of short-term volatility.</p>
      <div class="learn-rule">
        <div class="rule-title">ENTRY 1 — 30–40% of position (First Signal)</div>
        <div class="rule-body">Start small when the first bullish signal appears. This could be RSI turning up from oversold, a bullish MACD crossover, or price bouncing off support. You're "testing the water."</div>
      </div>
      <div class="learn-rule" style="border-color:var(--amber)">
        <div class="rule-title" style="color:var(--amber)">ENTRY 2 — 40% of position (Confirmation)</div>
        <div class="rule-body">Add your larger tranche when you get confirmation. Price holds support on a retest, volume confirms the move, RSI stays above 40. Now you're more confident.</div>
      </div>
      <div class="learn-rule" style="border-color:var(--blue)">
        <div class="rule-title" style="color:var(--blue)">ENTRY 3 — 20–30% of position (Breakout)</div>
        <div class="rule-body">The final add when price breaks out above resistance with volume. This is the most expensive entry but you're buying confirmed strength. Total position is now full.</div>
      </div>
      <h3>STOP LOSS — DEFINE YOUR RISK FIRST</h3>
      <p>Before buying, decide where you are WRONG. This is your stop loss. Calculate it as a percentage of your position. If you can't tolerate the loss from current price to stop, reduce your position size. Never move your stop loss down. Only move it up.</p>
      <h3>POSITION SIZING RULE</h3>
      <p>Risk no more than 1–2% of your total portfolio on any single trade. If your stop is 10% below entry, your max position size = 2% portfolio / 10% stop = 20% of portfolio. For moonshots with wider stops, reduce size proportionally.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <!-- 10 How to Build a Sell Plan -->

  <div class="learn-card">
    <div class="learn-hdr" onclick="toggleLearn(this)">
      <div class="learn-icon">💰</div>
      <div class="learn-title">HOW TO BUILD A SELL PLAN</div>
      <div class="learn-tag">STRATEGY</div>
      <div class="learn-arrow">›</div>
    </div>
    <div class="learn-body">
      <h3>STAGED PROFIT TAKING — T1/T2/T3</h3>
      <p>The hardest thing in investing is selling. Most investors sell too early (panic on dips) or too late (ride it all the way back down). A pre-built sell plan removes emotion.</p>
      <div class="learn-rule">
        <div class="rule-title">T1 — Sell 25–30% (First Target)</div>
        <div class="rule-body">Take some profit off the table when price hits the first resistance level or your first target. This locks in a guaranteed win and removes psychological pressure. You now "can't lose" your initial capital on this trade.</div>
      </div>
      <div class="learn-rule" style="border-color:var(--amber)">
        <div class="rule-title" style="color:var(--amber)">T2 — Sell 35–40% (Main Target)</div>
        <div class="rule-body">Your core sell zone. Based on the next major resistance level, Fibonacci extension, or analyst price target. This is where most of your gains are realized.</div>
      </div>
      <div class="learn-rule" style="border-color:var(--purple)">
        <div class="rule-title" style="color:var(--purple)">T3 — LET 25–30% RIDE (The Moonshot Tranche)</div>
        <div class="rule-body">Keep a small position for the extended move. For moonshots (CLOV at $10+, BTC at new ATH), this is where life-changing returns happen. Let this ride until the thesis breaks or price collapses back through major support.</div>
      </div>
      <h3>TAX AWARENESS (YOUR SITUATION)</h3>
      <p>As a US expat in Dubai, you still pay US capital gains tax. Positions held <strong style="color:var(--red)">&lt;12 months = 37% short-term tax</strong>. Held <strong style="color:var(--green)">&gt;12 months = 23.8% long-term tax</strong>. This 13.2% difference is massive on large gains. Always plan entries so you can hold to the 12-month mark if possible.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <!-- 11 Long-term strategy -->

  <div class="learn-card">
    <div class="learn-hdr" onclick="toggleLearn(this)">
      <div class="learn-icon">🌍</div>
      <div class="learn-title">LONG-TERM INVESTOR TA STRATEGY</div>
      <div class="learn-tag">YOUR APPROACH</div>
      <div class="learn-arrow">›</div>
    </div>
    <div class="learn-body">
      <h3>TA FOR PATIENT INVESTORS</h3>
      <p>You're not a trader. TA isn't about day-trading — it's about finding the <strong style="color:var(--green)">best possible entry point</strong> for a thesis you already believe in. The goal is to enter at strong support, hold through volatility, and exit when fundamentals or technicals break down long-term.</p>
      <div class="learn-rule">
        <div class="rule-title">YOUR FRAMEWORK — 4 QUESTIONS BEFORE EVERY BUY</div>
        <div class="rule-body">
          1. Is price above or below EMA200? (Trend direction)<br/>
          2. Is RSI in a reasonable zone, not extreme? (Entry timing)<br/>
          3. Is volume confirming the move? (Conviction)<br/>
          4. Is there a clear support level below entry? (Risk definition)
        </div>
      </div>
      <h3>HOW TO USE THIS TOOL</h3>
      <ul>
        <li>Load CLOV weekly to watch for accumulation patterns and support holds</li>
        <li>Load UNH to identify when the selloff creates a durable entry (EMA200 bounce)</li>
        <li>Load BTC to monitor whether we're in an accumulation zone (RSI + BB squeeze)</li>
        <li>Use the SIGNALS tab to get your buy/sell plan auto-generated for each asset</li>
        <li>Never act on one signal alone — wait for 3+ signals to align</li>
      </ul>
      <div class="learn-rule" style="border-color:var(--amber)">
        <div class="rule-title" style="color:var(--amber)">⚠️ THE MOST IMPORTANT RULE</div>
        <div class="rule-body">TA is a probability tool, not a crystal ball. It tells you where the best risk/reward setups are. Always combine TA with fundamental analysis and position sizing discipline. Your edge is patience — let the setup come to you.</div>
      </div>
    </div>
  </div>

  <div style="height:30px"></div>
</div>

</div>
